	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Telephone numbers in the United Kingdom</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"+44" redirects here. For the band, see <a href="/wiki/%2B44_(band)" title="+44 (band)">+44 (band)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

calling codes">Country calling code</a></th><td>+44</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/International_call_prefix" class="mw-redirect" title="International call prefix">International call prefix</a></th><td>00</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Trunk_prefix" title="Trunk prefix">Trunk prefix</a></th><td>0</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" codes</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Telephone numbers in the United Kingdom</b> are administered by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">UK government</a>'s Office of Communications (<a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a>). For this purpose Ofcom established a <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">telephone numbering plan</a>, known as the <i>National Telephone Numbering Plan</i>, which is the system for assigning <a href="/wiki/Telephone_number" title="Telephone number">telephone numbers</a> to subscriber stations.
</p><p>The numbers are of variable length. Local numbers are supported from land-lines, or numbers can be dialled with a '0'-lead prefix that denotes either a geographical region or another service. Cell phone numbers have their own prefixes which are not geographical and are completely portable between providers.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since 28 April 2001, almost all geographic numbers and most non-geographic numbers have 9 or 10 national (significant) numbers after the "0" <a href="/wiki/Trunk_prefix" title="Trunk prefix">trunk code</a>. All mobile telephone numbers have 10 national (significant) numbers after the "0" trunk code. The overall structure of the UK's National Numbering Plan is:<sup id="cite_ref-2003guide_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2003guide-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="col">Prefix
</th>
<th scope="col">Service type
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">00
</th>
<td>International
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">01
</th>
<td>Geographic area codes.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">02
</th>
<td>Geographic area codes (introduced in 2000).
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">03
</th>
<td>Non-geographic numbers charged at standard geographic area code rates (introduced 2007).
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">04
</th>
<td>Reserved.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">05
</th>
<td>Corporate numbering and <a href="/wiki/Voice_over_IP" title="Voice over IP">VoIP</a> services (some VoIP services use 08 or geographic numbers). Freephone (toll free) on 0500 until June 2017.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">06
</th>
<td>Was reserved for possible use by <a href="/wiki/Personal_numbering" title="Personal numbering">personal numbering</a> (PNS) instead of 070 following <a href="/wiki/Consumer_confusion" title="Consumer confusion">consumer confusion</a> with mobile phones.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">07
</th>
<td>Mostly for mobile phones on 071xx, 072xx, 073xx, 074xx, 075xx, 07624, 077xx, 078xx, and 079xx. <a href="/wiki/Personal_numbering" title="Personal numbering">Personal numbering</a> on 070. Pagers on 076xx.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">08
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Toll-free_telephone_number" title="Toll-free telephone number">Freephone</a> (toll free) on 080, and Special Services (formerly known as local and national rate) on 084 and 087.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">09
</th>
<td>Premium Rate services (PRS).
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A short sample of geographic numbers, set out in the officially approved (<a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a>) number groups:<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>In the United Kingdom, area codes are two, three, four, or, rarely, five digits long (after the initial zero). Regions with shorter area codes, typically large cities, permit the allocation of more telephone numbers as the local number portion has more digits. Local customer numbers are four to eight figures long. The total number of digits is ten, but in a very few areas the total may be nine digits (after the initial zero). The "area code" is also referred to as an "STD (code)" (<a href="/wiki/Subscriber_trunk_dialling" title="Subscriber trunk dialling">subscriber trunk dialling</a>) or a "dialling code" in the UK.
</p><p>The code allocated to the largest population is (<a href="/wiki/020" title="020">020</a>) for <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. The code allocated to the largest area is (028) for all of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. The UK Numbering Plan also applies to three British <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a>—<a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>—even though they are not part of the UK itself.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format">Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <p>Possible number formats for UK telephone numbers are:
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Number length
</th>
<th>10 digit NSN
</th>
<th>9 digit NSN
</th>
<th>7 digit NSN
</th>
<th>6 digits
</th>
<th>4 digits
</th>
<th>3 digits
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th>Number formats
</th>
<td valign="top">(01xx xx)&#160;xxxxx<br />(01xxx)&#160;xxxxxx<br />(01x1) xxx xxxx<br />(011x) xxx xxxx<br />(02x) xxxx xxxx<br />03xx xxx xxxx<br />055 xxxx xxxx<br />056 xxxx xxxx<br />070 xxxx xxxx<br />07624 xxxxxx<br />076 xxxx xxxx<br />07xxx xxxxxx<br />0800 xxx xxxx<br />08xx xxx xxxx<br />09xx xxx xxxx
</td>
<td valign="top">(0169 77)&#160;xxxx<br />(01xxx)&#160;xxxxx<br />0500 xxxxxx<br />0800 xxxxxx
</td>
<td valign="top">0800 1111<br />0845&#160;46&#160;4x
</td>
<td valign="top">118xxx<br />116xxx
</td>
<td valign="top">1470<br />1471<br />1475<br />1477<br />1571
</td>
<td valign="top">999<br />112<br />111<br />123<br />101<br />105
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Number ranges starting 01 can have <a href="/wiki/National_Significant_Number" class="mw-redirect" title="National Significant Number">National Significant Number (NSN)</a> length as 10 or 9 digits. NSN is the number of digits after the leading 0 trunk code or +44 international prefix.The 0800 range can have NSN length as 10, 9 or 7 digits. The 0845 range can have NSN length as 10 or 7 digits. The 0500 range had NSN length as 9 digits only, and was withdrawn from use on 3 June 2017. All other UK numbers have NSN length of 10 digits. There are no telephone numbers in the UK with an NSN length of 8 digits.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_numbering">Geographic numbering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geographic numbering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_dialling_codes_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of dialling codes in the United Kingdom">List of dialling codes in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Standard_geographic_numbers">Standard geographic numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Standard geographic numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Geographic telephone numbers in the UK always have nine or ten digits after the 0 trunk code or +44 international dialling prefix.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-digit_area_codes">Four-digit area codes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Four-digit area codes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Four-digit area codes have either six-digit subscriber numbers or a mix of five- and six-digit subscriber numbers.
</p>
<ul><li><b>(01xxx)</b> xxxxxx</li></ul>
<p>This is the format used by most areas. It has a four-digit area code (after the initial zero) and a six digit subscriber number, and is known as 4+6 format. These area codes were changed by adding a "1" directly after the initial zero as a part of <a href="/wiki/PhONEday" title="PhONEday">PhONEday</a> in 1995. Just short of 581 areas use this format, and the area codes range from 01200 to 01998. Almost all (01xxx) area codes now have only six digit subscriber numbers, but a small number of these areas also have some subscriber numbers only five digits in length (see next section).
</p>

<p>Six of the four-digit area codes are known as "mixed" areas as they share those four digits with the twelve five-digit area codes. This leads to a restriction as to which initial digits can be used for subscriber numbers within those four-digit area codes, e.g. in the 01387 four-digit area code, subscriber numbers cannot begin with a 3 because 013873 is a separate five-digit area code; likewise in the 01946 four-digit area code, subscriber numbers cannot begin with a 7 because 019467 is a separate five-digit area code.
</p>
<ul><li><b>(01xxx)</b> xxxxx</li></ul>
<p>This is used for forty smaller towns which have a mixture of six and five digit local numbers, each type allocated in specific DE blocks*; e.g. in the 01647 area code numbers beginning 24 and 61 have five digits (24xxx and 61xxx; known as 4+5 format) whereas all other DE blocks* within that area code have six digit numbers. The number of places with five digit subscriber numbers and an 01xxx area code has declined rapidly in recent decades. There were 511 ranges allocated across 56 different area codes in January 1998. The <a href="/wiki/Big_Number_Change" title="Big Number Change">Big Number Change</a> removed many, especially in Northern Ireland, and by July 2005 there were only 329 ranges in 42 codes. By April 2010 this had reduced to 324 ranges in 40 codes, with still the same number in November 2012. The 40 area codes are listed in the table below.
</p><p>*A DE block is a block of numbers where (taking the area code and the subscriber number together) the initial 0 and the next six digits after it are the same for all the subscriber numbers in the block.
</p><p>(These area codes, like many others, were changed by adding a "1" directly after the initial zero as a part of PhONEday in 1995.)
</p>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Three-digit_area_codes">Three-digit area codes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Three-digit area codes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Three-digit area codes always have seven-digit subscriber numbers and always begin 011x or 01x1.
</p>
<ul><li><b>(01x1)</b> xxx xxxx</li></ul>
<p>This is the geographic number format for the first round of five large cities moved to <a href="/wiki/All_figure_dialling" class="mw-redirect" title="All figure dialling">all figure dialling</a> in the 1960s, and subsequently also used in the metropolitan county of Tyne and Wear, eastern County Durham and south-eastern Northumberland from the 1980s onwards. These six areas have a three-digit area code matching the pattern <i>1x1</i> (after the initial zero) and a seven digit subscriber number, and this is known as 3+7 format. These area codes were changed by adding a "1" directly after the initial zero as a part of PhONEday in 1995.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row">0121
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a></td>
<td>formerly 021 (2 = B)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0131
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a></td>
<td>formerly 031 (3 = E)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0141
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a></td>
<td>formerly 041 (4 = G)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0151
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a></td>
<td>formerly 051 (5 = L)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0161
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a></td>
<td>formerly 061 (6 = M)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0171
</th>
<td colspan="2"><i>Used for <a href="/wiki/Inner_London" title="Inner London">Inner London</a> from 1990 until 2000</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0181
</th>
<td colspan="2"><i>Used for <a href="/wiki/Outer_London" title="Outer London">Outer London</a> from 1990 until 2000</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0191
</th>
<td>County of <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear" title="Tyne and Wear">Tyne and Wear</a>, eastern <a href="/wiki/County_Durham" title="County Durham">County Durham</a>,<br />south-eastern <a href="/wiki/Northumberland" title="Northumberland">Northumberland</a></td>
<td>formerly <a href="/wiki/History_of_telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom#All_figure_dialling" title="History of telephone numbers in the United Kingdom">091</a> (9 = tYne)
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li><b>(011x)</b> xxx xxxx</li></ul>
<p>This is the geographic number format for the second round of large cities and towns moved to brand-new three-digit area codes. Five of these were moved in 1995 as a part of <a href="/wiki/PhONEday" title="PhONEday">PhONEday</a>, with Reading then following a year later. At the time of the change, an extra digit was added to the subscriber number. These six areas have a three-digit area code matching the pattern <i>11x</i>, with a seven-digit subscriber number, and this is known as 3+7 format. The first three digits of the local number identifies a small area within the town or city. The former Reading area code had already been changed once, by adding a "1" directly after the initial zero as a part of PhONEday in 1995.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<td>formerly 0533 (53 = LE)

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Two-digit_area_codes">Two-digit area codes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Two-digit area codes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Two-digit area codes always have eight-digit subscriber numbers and always begin 02.
</p>
<ul><li><b>(02x)</b> xxxx xxxx</li></ul>
<p>This is the newest geographic number format. It is used for the third tier of large cities and for Northern Ireland, and was formed as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Number_Change" title="Big Number Change">Big Number Change</a> in 2000. The new area code is much shorter than the old one, and begins 02 unlike the previous 01 area codes. Numbers in these five areas are commonly <a href="/wiki/UK_telephone_code_misconceptions" title="UK telephone code misconceptions">misquoted</a>, e.g. London as 0207 or Cardiff as 02920. The numbers consist of a two-digit area code matching the pattern <i>02x</i>, and an eight-digit subscriber number, and this is known as 2+8 format.
</p><p>The first four digits of the local number identifies a small area within the town or city. At the time of the change, the subscriber part of the number gained an extra digit in London, those in Northern Ireland gained two or three digits, and the subscriber part of the number in the other areas gained two digits. All of these areas were also subject to a previous code change, one that added a "1" directly after the initial zero, as a part of PhONEday in 1995.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Five-digit_area_codes">Five-digit area codes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Five-digit area codes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Five-digit area codes have either five-digit subscriber numbers or a mix of four- and five-digit subscriber numbers.
Five-digit area codes always share their first four digits with four-digit area codes.
</p>
<ul><li><b>(01xx xx)</b> xxxxx and <b>(01xx xx)</b> xxxx</li></ul>
<p>This is the oldest geographic number format and is used for twelve smaller towns and villages where the subscriber number is either five or (in one area code) four digits long. These are known as 5+5 and 5+4 format. Therefore, the STD code and the subscriber number does not always total ten digits after the initial zero trunk code. These area codes were changed by adding a "1" directly after the initial zero as a part of PhONEday in 1995. The number of places using these two formats has declined rapidly in recent decades and Brampton is the last place in the UK with four-digit local numbers.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row">0138 73
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Langholm" title="Langholm">Langholm</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0152 42
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Hornby,_Lancashire" class="mw-redirect" title="Hornby, Lancashire">Hornby</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0153 94
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Hawkshead" title="Hawkshead">Hawkshead</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0153 95
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Grange-over-Sands" title="Grange-over-Sands">Grange-over-Sands</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0153 96

<td><a href="/wiki/Sedbergh" title="Sedbergh">Sedbergh</a>
</td></tr>

</td></tr>

</th>

</td></tr>

</th>

</th>

</td></tr>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The above twelve area codes and their six 'parent' area codes (01387, 01524, 01539, 01697, 01768 and 01946) are known as 'Mixed' areas due to multiple area codes sharing the same SABC digits (i.e. the initial zero and the following four digits).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National_dialling_only_ranges">National dialling only ranges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: National dialling only ranges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>These ranges have subscriber numbers beginning with the digits "0" or "1", e.g.:
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row">0169 77 0xxxx
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Brampton,_Carlisle" title="Brampton, Carlisle">Brampton</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">01332 050xxx
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Derby" title="Derby">Derby</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">01382 006xxx
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Dundee" title="Dundee">Dundee</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0141 005 xxxx
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0117 101 xxxx
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">0118 00x xxxx
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">020 0003 xxxx
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Currently, these numbers are mostly used as the termination points<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> for non-geographic numbers, and by some automated systems such as alarms. As such they are not usually meant to be directly dialled. These numbers have been problematic as some mobile phone operators in the UK do not allow access to these ranges,<sup id="cite_ref-servicelevel_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-servicelevel-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and there may also be difficulty accessing these numbers from outside the UK.
Regulator Ofcom proposes that in future these numbers be released for wider, general-purpose use in up to 70 area codes facing number shortage.<sup id="cite_ref-geonumbers_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geonumbers-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
In order to avoid confusion with codes beginning with these digits, the area code must always be dialled, even from within the same geographic exchange. Accordingly, if these numbers are eventually released for general use, Ofcom proposes completely removing the ability to dial locally without the area code in areas affected. This occurred on 1 November 2012 for the 01202 area code, which covers <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth" title="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recently, the carrier TalkTalk have inadvertently released parts of the <b>020 0011</b> range to the general public,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> with these numbers currently being in use. For example, the charity Give a Car used the number 020 0011 1664 for a while, but recently switched to a proper London number.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_telephones">Mobile telephones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mobile telephones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>07xxx</b> xxxxxx—mobile phones and WiFi numbers.</li></ul>
<p>Individual mobile phone companies are allocated different ranges within the <b>073xx</b>, <b>074xx</b>, <b>075xx</b>, <b>07624</b>, <b>077xx</b>, <b>078xx</b> and <b>079xx</b> area codes. Changes to mobile phone numbers in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Number_Change" title="Big Number Change">Big Number Change</a> were mostly straight replacements, such as <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_UK" title="Vodafone UK">Vodafone</a> customers on the <b>03</b>78 block became <b>077</b>78.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>071xx</b>&#160;xxxxxx
</th>
<td>Mobile Phones (in use since January 2017)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>073xx</b>&#160;xxxxxx
</th>
<td>Mobile phones (in use since November 2014)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>074xx</b>&#160;xxxxxx
</th>
<td>Mobile phones (in use since November 2009)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>075xx</b> xxxxxx
</th>
<td>Mobile phones (in use since May 2007)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>07624</b> xxxxxx
</th>
<td>Mobile phones on the Isle of Man
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>077xx</b> xxxxxx
</th>
<td>Mobile phones (former 03xx and 04xx—mostly <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_UK" title="Vodafone UK">Vodafone</a> and <a href="/wiki/O2_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="O2 (United Kingdom)">O2 (formerly Cellnet)</a>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>078xx</b> xxxxxx
</th>
<td>Mobile phones (former 05xx, 06xx and 08xx—mostly <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_UK" title="Vodafone UK">Vodafone</a> and <a href="/wiki/O2_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="O2 (United Kingdom)">O2 (formerly Cellnet)</a>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>079xx</b> xxxxxx
</th>
<td>Mobile phones (former 09xx—mostly <a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Limited">EE</a> (formerly  <a href="/wiki/Orange_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Orange (UK)">Orange</a> and <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_UK" title="T-Mobile UK">one2one)</a>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>07911</b> 2xxxxx <br /> <b>07911</b> 8xxxxx
</th>
<td>WiFi numbers (e.g. 3G/LTE-enabled tablet computers)
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Since the advent of <a href="/wiki/Mobile_number_portability" title="Mobile number portability">Mobile number portability</a>, mobile phone number prefixes can no longer be relied on to determine the current operator of a particular mobile phone &#8211; only the original operator.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pagers_and_personal_numbering">Pagers and personal numbering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Pagers and personal numbering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>07x</b> xxxx xxxx—pagers and <a href="/wiki/Personal_numbering" title="Personal numbering">personal numbering</a> (PNS).</li></ul>
<p>070 and 076 numbers are often charged at a much higher rate than calling the similar-looking 07xxx mobile telephone numbers.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>070</b>&#160;xxxx&#160;xxxx
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Personal_numbering" title="Personal numbering">Personal numbering</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>076</b> xxxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Pagers (excluding 07624, used for mobile phones on the Isle of Man)
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Personal numbers beginning 070 are regulated by <a href="/wiki/Phone-paid_Services_Authority" title="Phone-paid Services Authority">Phone-paid Services Authority</a>.
</p><p>From 1 October 2019, Ofcom is capping the termination or wholesale rate for calls to 070 numbers to be at the same level as for calls to mobile numbers. Ofcom "<i>expect[s] this will allow phone companies to price calls to these numbers or include them in call allowances in the same way that they do for calls to mobile [number]s</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-ofcom_costs_070_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ofcom_costs_070-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-geographic_numbering">Non-geographic numbering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Non-geographic numbering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Non-geographic_telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Non-geographic telephone numbers in the United Kingdom">Non-geographic telephone numbers in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-geographic_numbers_charged_at_geographic_rate">Non-geographic numbers charged at geographic rate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Non-geographic numbers charged at geographic rate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><b>03xx</b> xxx xxxx—<a href="/wiki/UK-wide_numbers" class="mw-redirect" title="UK-wide numbers">"UK-wide" numbering</a>.</li></ul>
<p>On 27 July 2006, <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a> announced that companies will soon be able to use an "03" non-geographic number, in place of other non-geographic numbers (such as <a href="/wiki/0870" class="mw-redirect" title="0870">0870</a> or <a href="/wiki/0845" class="mw-redirect" title="0845">0845</a> numbers). Callers would be charged at the same rate as if they were calling a geographic number (01 or 02).<sup id="cite_ref-ofcom-09prs_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ofcom-09prs-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This means that customers who are benefiting from inclusive minutes on mobile phone or landline calling plans would also be able to call these numbers using their inclusive minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-intro03numbers_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intro03numbers-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> On 13 February 2007, Ofcom released more details on their plans for the 03 range and announced that allocations of 03 numbers to providers would begin in March 2007. Whilst 01, 02 and 07 numbers can receive text messages, currently the majority of cellular network providers do not support the sending of text messages to 03 numbers. Three different ranges of numbers were announced; those beginning 030x are reserved for qualifying public bodies and non-profit organisations, those beginning 033x, which are available for allocation to anyone, and those beginning 034x and 037x which will be used for migration from the matching 084x and 087x number ranges respectively. Ofcom itself began using 03 numbers on 13 November 2007 for public use.<sup id="cite_ref-contactOfcom_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-contactOfcom-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><a href="/wiki/UK-wide_numbers" class="mw-redirect" title="UK-wide numbers"><b>030x</b>&#160;xxx&#160;xxxx</a>
</th>
<td>For qualifying public bodies and non-profit organisations as defined by Ofcom
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>033x</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>For any end user
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>034x</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Migration range for operators who have 084x numbers
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>037x</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Migration range for operators who have 087x numbers
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_and_VoIP_numbering">Corporate and VoIP numbering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Corporate and VoIP numbering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><b>05x</b> xxxx xxxx—Corporate and VoIP numbering.</li></ul>
<p>Unlike 03 numbers there is no uniform pricing for 05 numbers; BT charge a number of different rates depending on the number dialled.<sup id="cite_ref-BTpriceS2P11_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BTpriceS2P11-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Some are charged at geographic rate, others not. Other operators are not required to charge the same rates as BT for calling 05 numbers.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>055</b>&#160;xxxx&#160;xxxx
</th>
<td>Corporate Numbering (but also used by BT for its Broadband Voice service)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>056</b> xxxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Allocated by Ofcom for LIECS (Location Independent Electronic Communications Services), e.g. <a href="/wiki/Voice_over_IP" title="Voice over IP">VoIP</a> services
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Freephone_numbers">Freephone numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Freephone numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><b>0500</b>&#160;xxxxxx—<a href="/wiki/Toll-free_telephone_number" title="Toll-free telephone number">Freephone</a> services allocated before 1999.</li></ul>
<p>Until July 2017, the <b>0500</b> range was used for some freephone services which were originally provided by <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Communications" title="Mercury Communications">Mercury Communications</a> Ltd (now <a href="/wiki/Cable_%26_Wireless_Worldwide" title="Cable &amp; Wireless Worldwide">Cable &amp; Wireless Worldwide</a>). These numbers were different from the rest of the 05 range in that they are only 9 digits in length after the 0 trunk code, e.g. 0500&#160;007&#160;007 (<a href="/wiki/National_Savings_and_Investments" title="National Savings and Investments">National Savings and Investments</a>), 0500&#160;2&#160;88&#160;2&#160;91 (<a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">BBC Radio 2</a>, 88 to 91 FM), 0500&#160;600&#160;600 (<a href="/wiki/Crimewatch" title="Crimewatch">Crimewatch</a>), 0500&#160;600&#160;700 (Watchdog<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>), and 0500&#160;909&#160;693 (<a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">BBC Radio 5 Live</a>, 909 and 693&#160;kHz). Numerous universities, government departments, airlines, banks and businesses also used these numbers. They were allocated before the general trend of using longer numbers started in 1997 and long before the rest of the 05 range was assigned to corporate and VoIP numbering after 2000.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0500</b>&#160;xxxxxx<sup id="cite_ref-0500code_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-0500code-18">&#91;notes 2&#93;</a></sup>
</th>
<td>Special Services - No charge to Customer a.k.a. "<a href="/wiki/Toll-free_telephone_number" title="Toll-free telephone number">Freephone</a>"
</td>
<td>Free to call from landline, up to 40p per minute from mobile.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The range was withdrawn by Ofcom in July 2017<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> as a result of a series of consultations starting from 2012<sup id="cite_ref-ofcom0500cons_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ofcom0500cons-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b>0800</b>&#160;xxxxxx, <b>0800</b>&#160;xxx&#160;xxxx and <b>0808</b>&#160;xxx&#160;xxxx—Freephone services.</li></ul>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0800</b>&#160;xxxxxx<sup id="cite_ref-0800code_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-0800code-21">&#91;notes 3&#93;</a></sup>
</th>
<td rowspan="3">Special Services - No charge to Customer a.k.a. "<a href="/wiki/Toll-free_telephone_number" title="Toll-free telephone number">Freephone</a>"
</td>
<td rowspan="3">Free to call from landline, and was up to 40p per minute from mobile, until July 2015 when calls to 080 numbers from mobiles became free. Calls to certain charity and similar services were always free from most mobiles.<br /><b>0808</b> 9xx xxxx numbers are used by freephone internet services.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Non-geographic_telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom#0500,_0800_and_0808_prefix" title="Non-geographic telephone numbers in the United Kingdom"><b>0800</b> xxx xxxx</a>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0808</b> xxx xxxx
</th></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There is one short "special" number in this range, <b>0800&#160;1111</b> for Childline.
</p><p>Additionally, numbers in the range 0808&#160;80x&#160;xxxx are reserved for not-for-profit helplines and as such are usually free to call from most mobile telephones. A number of other numbers can also called for free from mobiles,<sup id="cite_ref-voda-free_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-voda-free-22">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-O2-free_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O2-free-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-virgin-free_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-virgin-free-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tmobile-free_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tmobile-free-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-orange-charity_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orange-charity-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-orange-free_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orange-free-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dwp-150110_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwp-150110-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-orange-dwp_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orange-dwp-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> but this varies by network.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fixed-rate_or_special-rate_services">Fixed-rate or special-rate services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fixed-rate or special-rate services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><b>084x</b> xxx xxxx (Special Services basic rate) – non-geographic fixed-rate or special-rate services</li>
<li><b>087x</b> xxx xxxx (Special Services higher rate) – non-geographic fixed-rate or special-rate services.</li></ul>
<p>With the exception of 080x freephone numbers, 08xx numbers are charged above geographic rates, with some of the extra revenue going to the terminating telco. This additional revenue may be shared with the subscriber, but is often used instead to subsidise additional network services, such as <a href="/wiki/Fax" title="Fax">fax</a>-to-<a href="/wiki/Email" title="Email">email</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virtual_office" title="Virtual office">virtual office</a> applications, call queuing, voicemail and easy number redirection. None of these call management services is exclusive to 08xx numbers, and they could be provided on any number range.
</p><p>Special Services basic rate range:
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0845</b>&#160;xxx&#160;xxxx
</th>
<td>Up to 5p a minute, varies daytime/evening/weekend, from BT landline, other providers may charge more; up to 42p a minute from mobiles.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0844</b> 00x xxxx
</th>
<td>Non-BT Discount Scheme—Internet Services incorporating unmetered access up to and including 5p for BT customers
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0844</b> 01x xxxx<br />to<br /><b>0844</b> 09x xxxx
</th>
<td><i>currently unused</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0844</b> 1xx xxxx
</th>
<td><i>currently unused</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0844</b> 2xx xxxx<br />to<br /><b>0844</b> 9xx xxxx
</th>
<td>Up to 4.26p a minute (plus VAT), varies daytime/evening/weekend, from BT landline, other providers may charge more; up to 42p a minute from mobiles.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0843</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Up to 4.26p a minute (plus VAT), but fixed (e.g. always 3p/minute or always 4p/minute) from BT landline, other providers may charge more; up to 42p a minute from mobiles.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0842</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Up to 4.26p a minute (plus VAT), but fixed (e.g. always 3p/minute or always 4p/minute) from BT landline, other providers may charge more; up to 42p a minute from mobiles.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There were a few short "special" number in this range, such as <b>0845 46 47</b> for NHS Direct; this was closed in 2014 and replaced by <a href="/wiki/NHS_111" title="NHS 111">NHS 111</a> except in Wales, where the transition took place in 2015.
</p><p>Special Services higher rate range:
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0870</b>&#160;xxx&#160;xxxx
</th>
<td>Up to 8p a minute (plus VAT), varies daytime/evening/weekend (charged at no more than the caller would pay for a call to a Geographic Number) from landline; up to 42p a minute from mobiles.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0871</b> 0xx xxxx
</th>
<td>Internet Services metered access, up to and including 10p/minute for BT customers.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0871</b> 1xx xxxx
</th>
<td><i>currently unused</i>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0871</b> 2xx xxxx<br />to<br /><b>0871</b> 9xx xxxx
</th>
<td>Up to 8.5p a minute (plus VAT) but fixed (e.g. always 6p/minute or always 8.5p/minute) from BT landline, other providers may charge more; up to 50p a minute from mobiles.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0872</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Up to 8.5p a minute (plus VAT) but fixed (e.g. always 6p/minute or always 8.5p/minute) from BT landline, other providers may charge more; up to 50p a minute from mobiles.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0873</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Up to 8.5p a minute (plus VAT) but fixed (e.g. always 6p/minute or always 8.5p/minute) from BT landline, other providers may charge more; up to 50p a minute from mobiles.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The usage of <b>0871</b>, <b>0872</b> and <b>0873</b> numbers is regulated by <a href="/wiki/PhonepayPlus" class="mw-redirect" title="PhonepayPlus">PhonepayPlus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PP_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PP-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is widespread confusion about the cost of calling 084 and 087 numbers. They often do not qualify for discounts and bundled minutes, and can be prohibitively expensive when called from mobiles and payphones. Many major companies persist in misdescribing them as "Local Rate", "Lo Call" (often as 'locall rate' which can be easily misread as 'local rate') or "National Rate" for which the <a href="/wiki/Advertising_Standards_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Advertising Standards Authority (United Kingdom)">Advertising Standards Authority</a> can take action.<sup id="cite_ref-asa-39577_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asa-39577-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asa-40724_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asa-40724-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asa-42507_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asa-42507-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asa-43684_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asa-43684-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asa-39587_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asa-39587-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asa-41766_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asa-41766-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asa-44430_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asa-44430-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cap-onandon_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cap-onandon-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cap-2005_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cap-2005-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cap-alert_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cap-alert-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cap-08_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cap-08-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
<sup id="cite_ref-cap-0845_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cap-0845-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cap-084_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cap-084-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cap-084_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cap-084-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cap-087_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cap-087-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the future, it is likely<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="still future? &quot;likely&quot;? (April 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that users of 084 and 087 numbers will have to declare the service charge element of the call cost when advertising their phone number, whilst telecoms companies will need to inform their customers about their access charge for calling each number range. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/EU_Consumer_Rights_Directive" class="mw-redirect" title="EU Consumer Rights Directive">EU Consumer Rights Directive</a> requires that many entities that held 084 and 087 numbers will no longer be allowed to use them. The directive bans the usage of numbers that cost more than calling a geographic number for customer service and complaints lines, and other such purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-bis_crd_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bis_crd-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eu-2011-83_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eu-2011-83-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1 July 2015, the charge for calls to 084, 087, 09 and 118 numbers is split into two parts: An access charge (payable to the company you make your phone calls with - e.g. BT, EE, Sky, etc.) and a service charge (the part of the call that goes to the company offering the service).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_08xx_number_ranges">Other 08xx number ranges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other 08xx number ranges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><b>08xx</b> xxx xxxx—Internet for schools and Inbound routing codes.</li></ul>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0820</b>&#160;xxx&#160;xxxx
</th>
<td>Special Services: Internet for schools
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0899</b>&#160;9xx&#160;xxxx
</th>
<td>Inbound routing codes
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span id="Premium_rate_content_services_.28PRS_and_SES.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Premium_rate_content_services_(PRS_and_SES)">Premium rate content services (PRS and SES)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Premium rate content services (PRS and SES)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><b>09xx</b> xxx xxxx—Premium Rate Content Services</li></ul>
<p>Numbers in the 09xx range are charged at the highest rates of any calls within the United Kingdom, and are controlled by various regulations regarding their use. The regulator is <a href="/wiki/PhonepayPlus" class="mw-redirect" title="PhonepayPlus">PhonepayPlus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PP_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PP-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> There are a large number of charge bands, some with high pence-per-minute rates, others with a high fixed-price for the entire call.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="width: auto; margin-left: 1.5em;">

<tbody><tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>090x</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Premium rate content services (PRS)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>0908</b> xxx xxxx<br /><b>0909</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Sexual entertainment services (SES) (not available for new allocations)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>091x</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Premium rate non-content services (PRS)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="font-weight: normal;"><b>098x</b> xxx xxxx
</th>
<td>Sexual entertainment services (SES)
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The earlier unused 092x xxx xxxx - 099x xxx xxxx allocation for "Broadband Internet Services" no longer exists and was removed from the number plan in 2005.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crown_dependencies">Crown dependencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Crown dependencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Although calls from UK landlines to landlines in the islands are charged at the same rate as those to other UK landlines (i.e. they are not treated as international calls), calls may be excluded from calling plans offering unlimited UK fixed line calls.
</p><p>Mobile operators may also charge more for calls to the islands and these calls are usually excluded from calling plans. Calls and SMS messages sent to island mobile phone numbers are not charged at the same rate as calls to UK mobile phone numbers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guernsey">Guernsey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Guernsey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Isle_of_Man">Isle of Man</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Isle of Man">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>On the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, both fixed (01624) and mobile phone (07624) numbers can be dialled locally in the six-digit format.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fictitious_numbers">Fictitious numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Fictitious numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ofcom has also reserved certain number ranges for use in television dramas and films, so as to avoid the risk of people having their telephone numbers displayed, and receiving unwanted calls. This is similar to the use of <a href="/wiki/Fictitious_telephone_number" title="Fictitious telephone number">fictitious telephone numbers</a> in the United States and Canada starting with the digits <b><a href="/wiki/555_telephone_number" class="mw-redirect" title="555 telephone number">555</a></b>.
</p><p>In most of the large cities with three-digit area codes a range of numbers is reserved, usually all the numbers starting with the digits <b>496</b>. For fictitious numbers in other areas the area code <b>01632</b> is reserved; this code is not in use, although 0632 was used for <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle upon Tyne</a> until the late 1980s (63 = NE) and briefly reallocated for use by premium rate services in the 1990s. There are also reserved ranges for fictitious mobile, freephone, and premium rate numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-nb38-drama1999_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nb38-drama1999-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-drama2004_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drama2004-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Post Office even produced dial centre labels for use in advertisements and film/TV with a mythical exchange called VINcent plus four digits. The numerical equivalent of VIN was 846 and all the caller got was the speaking clock (i.e. 846 is also numerical equivalent of TIM) in the big city "Director" areas.<sup id="cite_ref-reynolds-numbers_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reynolds-numbers-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At around the same time as the other <a href="/wiki/Big_Number_Change" title="Big Number Change">Big Number Change</a> changes, Ofcom revised their recommendations to update the prefixes, add additional areas, and increase the size of the allocation from 10 to 1000 numbers per block. Those changes are listed in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Number_Change#Numbers_for_drama" title="Big Number Change">Big Number Change</a> article.
</p><p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Coronation_Street" title="Coronation Street">Coronation Street</a></i>, the fictional Manchester suburb of Weatherfield uses the unallocated range (0161) 715 xxxx.<sup id="cite_ref-sabcde4xls_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sabcde4xls-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_service_numbers">Special service numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Special service numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_services_and_helplines">Emergency services and helplines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Emergency services and helplines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The UK has two free emergency numbers—the traditional <b>999</b>, which is still widely used, and the EU standard <b>112</b>, which can be used in all member states of the European Union. Both <a href="/wiki/999_(emergency_telephone_number)" title="999 (emergency telephone number)">999</a> and <a href="/wiki/1-1-2" class="mw-redirect" title="1-1-2">112</a> are used to contact all emergency services: Police, Fire Service, Ambulance Service, and Coastguard. (Standard advice for Mountain Rescue or Cave Rescue is to ask the emergency operator for the police, who oversee the communication with these two services.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>)
</p><p>Both numbers can be called from mobile phones with the keylock on, or without entering the PIN where that would otherwise be required. Although some mobile phones allow emergency calls to be attempted without a SIM card, at present the UK networks reject such calls. Since November 2009, an emergency call can be made through any UK mobile network as long as there is a SIM for any valid UK network in the handset. Although UK VOIP phone providers are required to offer 999 / 112 service this is subject to a registration for the service and with a verified service address and users need to be aware such service may not work in a power blackout; However International VOIP providers may not provide this service.
</p><p>The chargeable number <b><a href="/wiki/Police_101" title="Police 101">101</a></b> was introduced for non-urgent crime and community safety calls on a trial basis in 2006. In Wales, the scheme was taken forward by all four police forces, who adopted the number for non-emergency calls on a permanent basis in early 2009. In England the scheme was on trial until 2012, when it was adopted nationwide and the cost to call changed from 10p per call to 15p per call. In Northern Ireland, the number was introduced by the <a href="/wiki/Police_Service_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Police Service of Northern Ireland">Police Service of Northern Ireland</a> in March 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The operator is obtained via <b>100</b> from landlines, while <a href="/wiki/Directory_enquiries" class="mw-redirect" title="Directory enquiries">directory enquiries</a>, formerly <i>192</i>, is now provided in the <b>118xxx</b> range, e.g. 118 212, 118 800, 118 500, <a href="/wiki/118_118_(UK)" title="118 118 (UK)">118 118</a>, by different companies. International Operator assistance is reached through <b>155</b>.
</p><p>From early 2010, the pan-European <b>116</b> number range came into use for social helplines. The first three numbers allocated were <a href="/wiki/Missing_People" title="Missing People">Missing People</a> using <b>116 000</b> for a missing children helpline, the NSPCC <a href="/wiki/ChildLine" class="mw-redirect" title="ChildLine">ChildLine</a> on <b>116 111</b>, and <a href="/wiki/Samaritans_(charity)" title="Samaritans (charity)">Samaritans</a> using <b>116 123</b> for an emotional support helpline. A recent consultation for the numbers 116 106 and 116 117 has yet to see any result.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service_(England)" title="National Health Service (England)">National Health Service</a> (NHS) can be reached on <b>111</b> for non-emergency calls (from landlines and mobiles only). In other European countries the number 116 117 is used for a similar purpose.
</p><p>Local <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_distribution" title="Electric power distribution">electricity network operators</a> can be reached on <b><a href="/wiki/105_(telephone_number)" title="105 (telephone number)">105</a></b> to report power cuts.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Two telephone helplines within the regular code space have only eight digits, namely <b>0800 1111</b> for <a href="/wiki/ChildLine" class="mw-redirect" title="ChildLine">ChildLine</a> and <b>0845 4647</b> for <a href="/wiki/NHS_Direct" title="NHS Direct">NHS Direct</a> in Wales.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Speaking_clock">Speaking clock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Speaking clock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the mid-1990s <a href="/wiki/Speaking_clock" title="Speaking clock">speaking clock</a> services have been available throughout Britain using the number <b>123</b>. Before this, exchanges in "Director" areas (Birmingham, Edinburgh, Glasgow, Liverpool, London and Manchester) dialled 846 (TIM), later changing to 123, and main exchanges in "non-Director" areas originally used "952", later changing to "80" with the introduction of STD and eventually to "8081" as other recorded services were introduced on 80X1 codes. Some mobile operators allocate other services to 123—such as customer services or voicemail etc.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automated_services_and_access_codes">Automated services and access codes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Automated services and access codes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Short codes beginning with <b>1</b> are reserved for telecom service providers' own functionality; some of the most well-known are codes for use with <a href="/wiki/Caller_ID" title="Caller ID">Caller Display</a>:
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin-left: 1.5em;">

</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>#31#
</th>
<td>Withhold number
</td>
<td>141 equivalent for use on mobile networks
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Many fixed line telephone subscribers, e.g. of BT,<sup id="cite_ref-elReg-20010629_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elReg-20010629-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Media" title="Virgin Media">Virgin Media</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NTLprice_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NTLprice-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> SkyTalk, <a href="/wiki/TalkTalk_(telecommunications_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="TalkTalk (telecommunications company)">TalkTalk</a>, and PlusNet, have the opportunity to use an automated messaging service which takes messages when the called number is either engaged ("busy") or not answered within a given time. This can be accessed by calling <b><a href="/wiki/1-5-7-1" title="1-5-7-1">1571</a></b>.
</p><p>For fixed line users, it is possible to override the carrier pre-selection (CPS) on a per-call basis, dialling a special code before the number, e.g. 1280 for BT, 1664 for LowerCall, or 1844 for Daisy. Ofcom defines the range for these as: "124 to 140, 143 to 146, 148 to 149, 160 to 169, and 181 to 189 inclusive. Numbers of up to 5-digits used to access an Indirect Access Provider (‘Type B Access Codes’)".<sup id="cite_ref-numberingplan_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-numberingplan-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="History of telephone numbers in the United Kingdom">History of telephone numbers in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Telephone_numbers_in_Overseas_Territories">Telephone numbers in Overseas Territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Telephone numbers in Overseas Territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Telephone numbers in British Overseas Territories do not come under the UK telephone numbering plan. These calls are treated as international calls. Below are the access codes for the overseas territories:
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">7 for two special 08xx numbers; 9 in some 01xxx areas, one 01xxxx area, all 0500 numbers, and some 0800 numbers; 10 in all other areas</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-0500code-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-0500code_18-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Older pre-PhONEday nine-digit 0500 numbers were left as nine-digit numbers after PhONEday. No new 0500 number ranges were released after PhONEday.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-0800code-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-0800code_21-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Older pre-PhONEday nine-digit 0800 numbers were left as nine-digit numbers after PhONEday. All new 0800 number ranges released after PhONEday have ten digits after the 0 trunk code.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 November</span> 2012</span>. <q>The Committee of Advertising Practice (CAP) ... has told advertisers who quote 084 and 087 numbers ... that they must not describe calls to those numbers as being charged at 'local' or 'national' rate. ... Calls made from other phone companies were often more expensive. BT has abolished its standard rate for the majority of its customers, making the description of calls being charged at 'local' or 'national' rate meaningless for them.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=CAP+News&amp;rft.atitle=Stop+the+call+confusion&amp;rft.date=2005-09-08&amp;rft.au=Committee+of+Advertising+Practice&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.cap.org.uk%2Fcap%2Fnews_events%2Fnews%2F2005%2FStop%2Bthe%2Bcall%2Bconfusion.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATelephone+numbers+in+the+United+Kingdom" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">Notes</th><td class="navbox-list navbox-even" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em">Numbers above can be dialled only from within the United Kingdom.
Numbers below can be dialled within the United Kingdom by prefixing with a 0 or with +44, and from outside the United Kingdom by prefixing with +44.</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">Geographic area codes</th><td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em">113<span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> <a href="/wiki/0114" title="0114">114</a><span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> 115<span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> 116<span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> 117<span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> 118
